Seems to count less &#34;ghost&#34; steps while riding in the car or moving in my desk chair, etc. 4. My history is viewable on the device itself with a simple backwards swipe of my finger. 5. The numbers it provides match up with my blood pressure cuff and takes just a few seconds. 7. Sleep tracker data seems to match how I FELT that I slept better than previously used trackers.  Comfortable wristband for that as well. 10. Elevation is grossly inaccurate. After a day of hiking 200 meters of elevation plus several floors of stairs, my pulse showed that I'd done 10 meters. 2. No correcting of sleep start and stop times on the website. Several times the sleep function has turned itself off prematurely (maybe I bumped the button?) or turned itself on during the day and once I forgot to turn it off  when I got up in the morning and it would have been useful in all cases to be able to manually correct the time in and out of bed. While 10,000 steps is recommended for the general population, I have an illness that sometimes keeps me from walking almost at all and other days 15,000 steps are within my capabilities.  More control over my goals would let me keep them realistic and attainable based on what's physically possible. 4. The screen can't easily be read in bright sun. Not a big deal, but if you're someone who likes to keep close tabs on what you're doing, every 30 minutes, the screen dullness may bother you.  Would I buy it again? Yes. I love the extra features this tracker has to offer. Do I hope they continue to improve it? YES! It would be near perfect in my eyes if it would allow manual entering of data (sleep) and personal step goals. If they change these features or fix the elevation counting issue, I'll come back to update.  Until then 4 stars for me.

006207377X|4.0|One Two Buckle My Shoe (also published under the title The Patriotic Murders) begins with the murder of a dentist, no doubt a piece of vicarious wish fulfillment for some readers.<br /><br />Although initially treated by the police as suicide, master detective Hercule Poirot, one of the dentist's last patients, has his suspicions from the beginning, and we eventually run through a cavalcade of suspects and red herrings before coming to a rather convoluted resolution to the mystery. But to me the most interesting thing about the book is not the Rube Goldberg solution but how the usually apolitical Agatha Christie gives us a glimpse of her politics, which seems to lean toward favoring conservative fiscal policy and established traditions over radical change to achieve some vision of social justice. Or at least that is what her hero Poirot seems to favor.<br /><br />It's interesting to contrast Christie with contemporaries like George Orwell and John Steinbeck, who were very much in favor of radical change and made no bones about it. Curiously, Christie's \\"coming out\\" is almost anachronistic, since One Two Buckle My Shoe was published (and I assume written) after World War II was well underway in Europe, effectively ending the period of the 20s and 30s when the direction of domestic policy could be debated in England and elsewhere with no outside distractions. With the start of war, those arguments were put on the back burner as simple national survival became the overriding consideration. In fact, the book was first serialized in America and published in book form in England just as the Blitz was raining bombs on English cities and the threat of Nazi invasion from across the Channel was a very real possibility. Under those circumstances, even Orwell was willing to put domestic squabbles aside in favor of defending the Homeland, as articulated in his contemporaneous essay My Country Right or Left.<br /><br />The other fascinating thing about One Two Buckle My Shoe is the continued evolution of Poirot. It has been my impression, as I am reading Christie's Poirot novels in chronological order, that Christie was starting to get tired of him at this point. In the three Poirot novels preceding One Two Buckle My Shoe (Appointment With Death, Hercule Poirot's Christmas, Sad Cypress) the little Belgian is somewhat minimized as Christie spends extra time on the other characters. In Christmas, despite getting title billing for the first time, Poirot is really little more than a plot device for solving the case rather than the focus of the narrative.<br /><br />But in One Two Buckle My Shoe, Poirot is clearly back in the forefront, and he is an especially forceful presence driving the story. He also ends up as the moral center. Christie also spends extra time rounding and humanizing him, humorously with his anxiety about visiting the dentist and almost poignantly with his \\"Am I getting too old?\\" questioning of himself at one point in the investigation. Well, turns out he isn't, or at least not took old to solve an intricate mystery, as this novel shows.he continued evolution of Poirot. It has been my impression, as I am reading Christie's Poirot novels in chronological order, that Christie was starting to get tired of him at this point. In the three Poirot novels preceding One Two Buckle My Shoe (Appointment With Death, Hercule Poirot's Christmas, Sad Cypress) the little Belgian is somewhat minimized as Christie spends extra time on the other characters. In Christmas, despite getting title billing for the first time, Poirot is really little more than a plot device for solving the case rather than the focus of the narrative.<br /><br />But in One Two Buckle My Shoe, Poirot is clearly back in the forefront, and he is an especially forceful presence driving the story. He also ends up as the moral center. Christie also spends extra time rounding and humanizing him, humorously with his anxiety about visiting the dentist and almost poignantly with his \\"Am I getting too old?\\" questioning of himself at one point in the investigation. Well, turns out he isn't, or at least not took old to solve an intricate mystery, as this novel shows.

B00BWBHIUG|4.0|This is a page-turner of a game, requiring continual interaction, so it's hard to put down.  Its clock keeps ticking overnight. There are reef plants and corals to purchase with \\"sand dollars\\" and \\"grow\\" with \\"algae\\". Mystery seeds become Rare Plants (but not always) to attract Rare Fish which will give Pearls in a day or three if you feed them algae. You can visit your friends' reefs, or random reefs, and work together on Co-op Quests.  Advance all the way to level 50 (original version had 40 levels), perhaps a level a day at first; it takes more and more points (Sea stars) to complete each level. Nemo and Dory and Ray give suggestions and little story lines. Follow the suggestions to gain stars to help advance to the next level. Occasional Challenges provide limited-edition Rare Fish, daily assignments keep the game going and earning star points.<br /><br />New Content appears sometimes, and if there's enough changes, a new Update is forced on you. The new version, 1.6.1 appeared at Amazon in May 2014; other platforms got it sooner. The update added Turtles Crush and Squirt, and new item spines (used to open chests.)  When there is a problem Disney Support has helped me.<br /><br />I'm on Android tablet with this game. You can get it for iPhone, iPad and Android phone.  There is a discussion group of users at gamesdreams.com which you should find and read before you spend all your pearls.  (It's too easy to use them, and buying more costs real money!) Pearls, algae and sand dollars can be bought for real money.  Treasure chests may yield pearls. The game requires Internet, and its server is sometimes down. B00DR0PDNE|4.0|3.5 stars for the price, form factor, ease of setup and works well with Netflix, Youtube and GooglePlay. Deduct some points for setup issue, can't play local contents (not Airplay-like) and lack of WOW factor. The product name, Chromecast, makes me think casting from Chrome browser is the key feature. It's not! TabCast on Chrome browser, is still in Beta and it doesn't support Android/iOS mobile device. As of now, it's really just a media streamer that allows Android/iOS/Windows mobile device<br />to select, play and control online contents from the 3 online video services mentioned above. This product is comparable to a Roku Streaming HDMI stick or Plair (home.plair.com), but definitely not in the category of wireless display (Miracast/WiDi) or DLNA/AirPlay media adapter.<br /><br />Below is my full hands on experience review against various devices, with different test cases and even at 2nd location.<br /><br />The Requirements<br /><br />For setup - I suggest to use a laptop, phone, or tablet and have it connected to your Wi-Fi router.  You should have the Wi-Fi PIN in handy. Depends on what you want to stream, you'll need to have either YouTube or Netflix app (and an account). Google Play is readily available on Android devices.<br /><br />Out-of-box Setup<br /><br />Even though the instruction printed on the packaging is very clear, the initial setup experience did not go smooth as I had expected. Connecting the HDMI dongle to the TV and USB cable for power was a piece of cake even my grandma can do. Once you've done that, the TV displays \\"Set me up\\" and instructs \\"On your laptop or phone, visit: google.com/chromecast/setup\\" with the setup name \\"ChromecastXXXX\\". However, it's setting the Wi-Fi connection that I encountered troubles and I think it could happen to other folks.<br />- I tried first with an Android phone, Nexus 4, the browser URL pointed to Google Play store to download and launch Chromecast app. It took a few tries for the app to detect and display my Chromecast, and then I was able to tell Chromecast to connect to my Wi-Fi router by providing it the PIN. Once I provided the wireless router's PIN, Chromecast then connects to the router and displays it's \\"Ready to Cast\\".<br />- On an iPad/iPhone, there is no Chromecast app available so the URL directs me to Google's online setup webpage. It's basically telling user to manually connect the phone Wi-Fi to the Chromecast device with SSID \\"ChromecastXXXX\\" and then configure its Wi-Fi setting to pair with the wireless router. It's good to have the Wi-Fi router's PIN in handy as you'll be asked to enter that information. Once that's configured, it connects to the Wi-Fi router and displays \\"Ready to Cast\\"<br />- On my laptop (Win8), Google setup site recommends to use the Chromecast utility to help with the setup. The utility works like a charm! It's almost like a wizard that could automatically extract the PIN from your existing Wi-Fi connection, connect to the Chromecast device, pushes the PIN to it and connects to the Wi-Fi router.<br /><br />The app is well designed and provides the best connection experience IMO.<br /><br />Note: If the system is connected to your Wi-Fi router via Cat-5 cable and your Wireless is turned off, then it will not be able to detect Chromecast.  Turn on the Wi-Fi and the app will be able to detect and connect to Chromecast.<br /><br />Streaming Experience<br /><br />Once the TV displays \\"Ready to Cast\\" screen, I was able to play online videos by touching the screen. Chromecast just figures out what video I want to play and then it pulls the content directly from the online content service's server. After a short ~5 seconds delay from the time I click play, the TV displays a buffering status and then plays the video without any hiccup. The video quality is probably 1080p or at least 720p - I'm not sure but it looked very clear. Once the movie is playing, I could make or receive phone call and do anything on the phone without affectingthe video stream on TV.<br />- Using Netflix app: The app works very well on both Nexus 4 and iPhone 5, but I've been seeing 'black screen of death' with Nexus 4 (Android 4.3) lately whenever I use Netflix [huge bug according to Android forums]. Netflix app displays the option for you to \\"Play on\\" ChromecastXXXX and will tell Chromecast to fetch the content from Netflix to display. I could rewind, forward and pause the video from the app, but I can't find a way to permanently stop the video. The volume can be controlled<br />from the app or from the volume button on the mobile device.  Netflix also allows you to toggle where you want the video play between the mobile device or TV, which is good because I start in one room and continue on another device from another room later. If there's another Chromecast TV in the house, I think it might be able to shift the video over there and continue where it left off. Since Netflix is the creator of the \\"DIAL\\" technology used in Chromecast so it's no surprise their app works so well.<br />- Youtube and GooglePlay: Similar streaming experience as Netflix, with the little cast-to-screen icon available on the app to Play On TV. I didn't use these apps as much so I don't know if there's any particular goods and bad.<br /><br />TabCast Experience<br /><br />I find this feature is OK, but not great as there are issues pending on the Wi-Fi environment and some websites. Noted the product description says support for \\"select web content through Chrome browser\\".  This feature is still in Beta as labeled on the plug-in, but not mentioned on the product webpage or Amazon's description. To use the feature, I need to download and install plug-in \\"GoogleCast\\".  Not to be confused with ChromeCast plug-in as it's taken by some 3rd party developer.  Once the plug-in is installed to Chrome browser, there's a Cast-to-TV icon showing on the right of the URL address bar. Click on icon allows me the option to \\"Cast this tab to...\\" and Chromecast device of my choice.  The max video quality supported is 720p coming from the browser tab and the computer needs to be at least an Core i5 CPU. I notice my laptop CPU is put to work when I stream from site like ABC/HULU/Vimeo as TabCast clones my browser page and mirrors to the TV.  The experience is odd as I can see what I browsed on the TV, but there's no mouse cursor.  There was noticeable latency as each click takes about 1-2 seconds for TV to update the images.  Nevertheless, both video and audio play on the TV via TabCast.<br />With Netflix and YouTube websites, there's a Cast-to option built-in to the player and the video gets retrieved directly from the device so the system is not put to work.  The supported video quality here is better since it's pulling directly from the service sites and does not go through many network hops.<br />There are certain times I notice a much bigger latency and my video disconnects in the middle of of playing while using TabCast.  This seems to be a Wi-Fi congestion problem or CPU overloads that the data has hard time traveling from laptop-to-router-to-Chromecast.  It is similar to the AppleTV Airplay (mirroring) feature and it also has some mixed reviews due to the many network hops issue.<br />Also TabCast plug-in is only available for Chrome browser on Windows/MAC system. The Chrome app on iOS does not allow you to TabCast since there's no plugin.  So the answer is No to the question \\"Can I cast a tab from phone or tablet's Chrome browser?\\"<br /><br />2nd Location / Portability<br /><br />It's such a small gadget (key fob size) that I was able to put in my pocket and took it to my friend's house.  I forgot to bring the USB micro cable, but good thing my friend had a USB micro cable available.  I'm not sure if Chromecast can be powered with an MHL-enabled HDMI port, but didn't matter since my friend's HDTV doesn't have MHL anyway.  Google doesn't mention about MHL support probably because the # of TVs with MHL is pretty low and most consumers don't even know about it.  The device powered on and looked for the previous wi-fi router connection, so I had to repeat the setup and provide the new wi-fi router's information.  Once it's connected and online, I was able to repeat the stream like I did at home.  I guess people can bring it on the road to hotels, but keep in mind the newer LCD/LED TVs at hotels don't allow people to change the HDMI input.  Also remember to bring the USB cable, power prong and get the Wi-Fi code for it to connect.<br /><br />Would I Recommend?<br />Yes, if you don't have Netflix or Youtube on your TV or Blu-ray player already.<br />No, if you're looking for a media player to stream local files from mobile devices or NAS on the network. Or looking to mirror anything from phone, tablet or laptop's screen to the TV<br /><br />Pros and Cons<br />Pros<br />- Setup app on PC is excellent and props for auto-grab of the existing Wi-Fi PIN feature.  Who remembers their Wi-Fi router PIN??<br />- On screen user friendly GUI<br />- The superb experience of browsing media on mobile device and hand off to Chromecast to play<br />- You can do other things on your mobile device while the video plays on TV, thus save battery<br />- Can stream from Netflix, YouTube and GooglePlay real well<br />- Control Chromecast with Netflix app trick mode is excellent, almost like a remote control<br />- The small compact sized form factor and USB power allows it to shut down when the TV is turned off<br />- The packaging, accessories and instructions<br />- The price! $35!? take my money Google even though I already have Netflix and YouTube built-in to my TVs and BD Player<br /><br />Cons<br />- Setup isn't smooth with mobile devices<br />- Can't permanently stop video on Netflix, thus may result to \\"over the allowed players limit\\" message on Netflix if you want to watch on a different device<br />- While using TabCast, someone can hijack the TV by sending video from Netflix/YouTube app or vice-versa (can be done from another room)<br />- TabCast is strictly for Windows/MAC Chrome browser with plug-in.  Cannot cast a tab from phone or tablet with Chrome app.<br />- Chromecast can't handle 1080p while using TabCast ... even from a powerful system<br />- No support for local contents playback (i.e. photos, music and recorded video on mobile devices).  I hear you can install additional plug-in, Plex, to PC and move the file to the TV via Chromecast<br />- No DLNA DMP support, thus you can't push media contents from other places to Chromecast like you can with AppleTV (AirPlay)<br /><br />Tips<br />- Use Chromecast Windows/Mac utility to find out the firmware version<br />- Use the utility to Reset the device to Factory default setting - or press and hold the push button for 10 seconds<br />- Chromecast Wi-Fi is on 2.4GHz band.  If your Wi-Fi router is dual-band, it should support 2 SSIDs (2.4 and 5GHz).  Chromecast will only see the 2.4GHz SSID<br />- If your Wi-Fi router is a dual-band, ensure it's not in AP isolation mode<br />- If your router has MAC whitelisting - your Wi-Fi network allows this device and your Chromecast to join<br />- Ensure you are not connected to VPN

Tell me a fun story Dan Brown!<br /><br />That being said, The Lost Symbol was terrible.  The writing style was \\"okay,\\" but didn't contribute to how bad the book was; rather, it failed because of (i) poor narrative; (ii) lack of cohesion between primary elements of the story; (iii) lack of character development; and (iv) predictability.<br /><br />The narrative was poor primarily because there were many chapters that did not make sense in relation to the story, or were unnecessarily included. Just one example was early on when Peter is telling his sister Kathrine--who is supposedly a \\"scientist\\"--about how the \\"ancients\\" somehow had knowledge of modern findings in fields such as theoretical physics.  Not only was this entire discussion unnecessary for the plot, it was just factually wrong.  Brown (through his character Peter) supports \\"claims\\" that modern science is merely \\"rediscovering\\" ancient knowledge, supporting these claims on the basis of vagaries and nonsense. For example, Brown (through Peter) explains that ancient mystics purported some notion of \\"extra\\" dimensions of thought, and this was somehow predictive of modern rigorous results from String Theory.  Not only is that plain wrong, demonstrating Brown's lack of understanding, it takes you out of the story because it seems like an argument a child would conceive to explain something he/she doesn't understand.  If Brown had consulted a real scientist, he would have likely dropped the whole \\"Noetic\\" thing, too. It's implausible passages and plot anchors like these that detract so strongly from the story.<br /><br />In the book, the CIA acts as a police force, which, surprisingly, it is not.  This is absurd, and it would have been more believable if the FBI had been substituted for the CIA. Why didn't his editor bring this up?<br /><br />There is also not much in the way of character development.  After so many books, I would expect his Robert Langdon character to be more developed.  I guess not.  Supposedly being a professor at Harvard university, Langdon is surprisingly dimwitted.  He often is the last to \\"get\\" things that he should get straight away.  I see this as a failing on Dan Brown's part; Brown can only write characters as intelligent as he is.<br /><br />Finally, the whole story is predictable early on after only a little thought, and the ending is unsatisfying and \\"amateurish.\\"  It feels like a giant waste of time after Langdon learns what the \\"lost symbol\\" actually is, especially due to its predictability.

1416914285|4.0|I know that a lot of people are giving C. Clare a hard time - for plagiarizing, for having flat characters, for being predictable, etc, etc, etc. However, a lot of these people had previously read her fanfiction and seemed to have a problem with her copying other writer's work and putting them into those stories. Unfortunately, the majority of fanfiction writers do this. Having been an avid reader of fanfiction for quite some time, it's easy enough to know. That being said, I had NOT read any of those stories before beginning this series about a week ago. I started reading this series with no previous notions of Clare's writing style, characterizations or world building skills. And I have to say, I enjoyed this entire series a lot; I read the first four books in less than a week, and have purchased the fifth. I didn't want to read them at first because I thought they looked stupid. When I heard the movie was coming out in a few weeks, I decided to buy the first and read it, since I hate seeing movies based off books when I haven't read the book. And I wasn't disappointed.<br /><br />Many people have pointed out similarities between this world and Harry Potter. Well, yes, those are there if you look for them. And now that multiple people have pointed that out - I DO see it. But was that what I was thinking when I read the books? Was I sitting there thinking, \\"Oh, well that definitely came from HP.\\" No, I was enjoying them for what they are. If you compare every book you read to Harry Potter, you need to get a life because those books stole quite a few ideas from earlier fantasy books as well. There's only a limited number of original ideas out there, and you can't expect every writer to come up with a brilliant one for new every series. None of Clare's supernatural creatures are new, but with the supernatural being so popular these days, how could you?<br /><br />The story is fast paced and entertaining. The reviews on the back of the book (which are admittedly biased, since they aren't going to put bad reviews on the book cover itself) claim that the book draws you in and makes you want to finish the book. That is absolutely true. The writing is not the best, but again, this is YA literature from an author who started out as a fanfiction writer, not a professor with a degree in English Literature and Linguistics. I didn't find the characters boring and flat - they aren't the best characterized out there, no, but I wasn't expecting them to be either. Clary and Jace in particular seem to get a lot of flack for either being too perfect or too one dimensional. They're not complex mystery people, no, but in my experience, very few teenagers are. And for those people claiming Clary is vapid - did you read Twilight? Bella is by far a worse heroine, so flat and dull that the satirist website The Oatmeal just calls her \\"Pants\\". And I agree. At least Clary has some definite stances and beliefs. And I found Jace to be far more believable and real than a lot of other male romantic interests. At least he had some demons and clearly isn't perfect.<br /><br />A good thing about this book is that you won't want to put it down. Another is that it's set in the author's clearly beloved hometown. I liked that because it really made me feel like I was in NYC. She clearly knew the places she was describing. The bad things? Well, it is very fast paced. The first book takes place over the span of a week. Another is that she had a big opportunity to really emphasize the psychological struggles a lot of the characters go through, and I don't think she accomplishes it well. It is also quite predictable, as is the norm for YA fiction. In fact, show me one that ISN'T predictable, and I'd be surprised.<br /><br />I would suggest just buying the book and reading it if you are really interested enough to spend all the time reading these reviews. It's a good read. It's not my favorite series, but I was drawn in enough to read four out of the five available inunder a week, which is saying something. And just so you know, a bunch of people giving this book flack (not all, but some) say Twilight is better, which actually made me laugh out loud. This book isn't even comparable to that garbage - well, they do both have vampires and werewolves. Give it a chance! I'm certainly glad I did.

0718178130|4.0|This is a very funny and engaging story that had me hooked from the first page.  Don Tillman is a brilliant academic with Asperger's Syndrome.  He knows he's a little odd and has coped with people's reactions to him all his life.  However, it's now time to get married and his little quirks may pose a problem.  How will he find a wife who'll love him the way he is?  He decides to approach the task scientifically by developing a screening questionnaire to weed out incompatible partners.  All goes to plan until he meets Rosie.  According to his evolutionary worldview, Rosie is totally unsuitable - she smokes, dyes her hair, has trouble keeping to a schedule, and is vegetarian.  The only problem is that all of the best days of his life have involved spending time with Rosie, except for his visit to the Museum of Natural History which still ranks as No. 1.  Could Don Tillman be falling in love?<br /><br />This is a feel-good story with a lot of heart.  Although Don is certainly unusual, we can't help liking him.  Rosie also has her own baggage, as she enlists Don's help in finding her real father.  We see Don break out of his rigid routine as he stops at nothing to get DNA samples from the 30-plus likely father candidates.  But if he changes too much to win Rosie, will he lose some of what makes him original in the first place?<br /><br />Graeme Simsion's writing moves along at a cracking pace, with great dialogue that makes you keep turning the pages.  Although funny, there are also poignant moments as Don starts to wonder if he'll ever really be acceptable.  The main reason I didn't give it five stars is that I prefer books without swearing.  The F-word was used a number of times, though not overdone.  The first occurrence wasn't until about p. 45 and I was hooked by then.  I don't think anything would have been lost by omitting the swearing, but it didn't detract from the overall story.  I still wanted to find out what happened to Rosie and Don.  Sex is also mentioneda number of times, though there are no actual sex scenes.  Indeed, Don's \\"unusual\\" ways of handling romantic situations end up being superior to that of his \\"normal\\" friend Gene.<br /><br />This is a book about accepting those who are different from us, but Simsion does it in a way that doesn't descend into moralising.  It made me laugh, but also made me think.  If you like the TV show, The Big Bang Theory, you'll really enjoy this book.

B00DL479DS|5.0|This is an exquisite new Brian De Palma film. Passion is playful pure cinema, covering De Palma's common themes and visual styles (voyeurism, technology, obsession, manipulation, deception, guilt, beautiful femme fatale's, heightened performances, overt artificiality, deliberate tonal shifts & stylistic flourishes). Whilst the first half of the film plays as a seemingly straightforward corporate drama, replete with corporate backstabbing (with a brilliant, but frankly bonkers Pino Donaggio soft core score). All is not as it seems however, and the second half of the film takes on a completely different direction and moves into the realms of dreams within dreams and German expressionism with a trademark and quite wonderful split screen section involving Mallarm's/Dubussy's 'Afternoon of the Faun' ballet linking the poem/ballet to a key character and murder of another which tricks you about its timeline. There are images and adverts of the ballet shown prior to this, and the story behind Mallarm's poem (the awakening of a faun and the faun's encounters with several nymphs in a dreamlike oration) is central to both to the plot of the story & the character & motivations of Isabella. (Donaggio's score too transforms to riff's on Bernard Hermann's dramatic strings).<br /><br />Like so many De Palma films, this gets even better with multiple viewings as you realise and understand more what about what you have and haven't seen, what is and isn't real, & what is a dream or a re-awakening.<br /><br />Elements of other De Palma psychological thrillers (in particular Sisters, Dressed to Kill & Raising Cain) resonate throughout this film. Overall, fantastic fun.

B002BSHXJA|5.0|I will have to admit, I wasn't paying attention when this mono box set came out in 2009, and I had never gotten around to buying the stereo box set. I know, what kind of Beatles fan am I :-) Recently I listened to all of my 1987 stereo CDs and was reminded of how bad the audio quality was. The worst offender was my favorite Beatles record, Rubber Soul. The mix is terrible and this is after George Martin remixed it in 1987. Surely the mono mix in this box set would be better.<br /><br />After reading every review on this box set I took the plunge. I have been listening in chronological order and I have just finished listening to both the mono and 1965 stereo mixes of Rubber Soul. The 2009 mono Rubber Soul blows away the 1987 stereo mix and master. Rubber Soul in mono sounds like the record I always wanted to own. However, when listening to the 1965 stereo on the same CD I am truly puzzled. I can't figure out why George Martin felt the need to redo the stereo mix in 1987. To me the 2009 master of the 1965 stereo mix sounds about the same or better. And the 2009 master of the 1965 mix of Help also sounds pretty good. I don't get it.<br /><br />I know there is more to come for me, but I wanted to say that I am already sold on this mono box set. As many have said, the Beatles in mono sound more like a band, and I can agree with one reviewer that thought that the mono mixes sounded more three dimensional. I think the mix of voices and instruments blend better. Believe it or not, I can pick out the instruments better in mono.<br /><br />My second favorite Beatles record; Please, Please, Me; is one of the first four that appeared in mono in the 1987. Overall, these first four 2009 mono masters are smoother, more detailed, and generally sound more like analog than digital - a good thing. The Mono Master CDs with all the mono singles are also improved in both audio quality and mix. Without the hard panning on I Feel Fine and Day Tripper, these two songs sound more coherent. Paperback Writer is much more enjoyable in mono.<br /><br />I still have to finish listening to the rest of this box set, but for my money, this mono box set is the way to go. I already have Let It Be....Naked and I am picking up Abbey Road in stereo - my third favorite Beatles record. Abbey Road was well done in every way. I can't wait to hear Abbey Road re-mastered!<br /><br />For the older stuff, I think by listening to the Beatles in mono you can concentrate on the music without the dated production getting in the way. To each his own though. I would not throw stones at anyone who preferred the stereo re-masters. We are fortunate to have a choice.<br /><br />EDIT:<br />I have now gotten through the entire mono box set. My candidate for most improved album is the White Album. I think it is a combination of both the mono mix and the mastering. Some of the songs on the White Album have intentionally distorted instruments and vocals. Other songs are intended to be straight performances. I think the records hang together better in mono and with the better mastering I can better pick out the instances where the Beatles intended a sound to be distorted alongside one that is clear. This of course requires a decent audio system to discern. I have read on audiophile blogs that Jimi Hendrix music is a favorite test for high end systems. It is ironic that it sometimes takes a great audio system to sort out what some may consider noise. The Beatles always wanted be different and one way was in their choices in audio production. Case in point: Listen to the following music recorded at Abbey Road at the same time as the Beatles and with I suspect the same equipment. This Hollies album sparkles with new mastering but also, the original recordings were more straightforward - just a different approach to production.<br />[[ASIN:B00008AWNW Greatest Hits - The Hollies]]

0767919408|3.0|No, Bill Bryson's latest isn't odd or wacky. But just about every character in his book is.<br /><br />In One Summer America 1927, Bryson focuses on individuals and their accomplishments. Nearly every one was not only historically interesting, but downright weird. Charles Lindbergh was anti-social, Calvin Coolidge liked to have his scalp massaged with Vaseline while he ate breakfast, Lou Gehrig was unnaturally devoted to his mother. Of course, this makes for a fun and lively narrative.<br /><br />It's hard to say how much research Bryson did for this book because the review copy doesn't include bibliography or references, and there are few footnotes in the text. But if you are moderately interested in 20th century American history, you'll have come across much of this story before, and possibly recently. He tells the story of [[ASIN:0312429622 Fordlandia]], and [[ASIN:1400078458 The Lost City of Z]], of Babe Ruth and [[ASIN:0743268938 Lou Gehrig]], of [[ASIN:0425170411 Lindbergh]], [[ASIN:B00BDM500O Henry Ford]], and [[ASIN:1416580603 Al Capone]]. There's a large supporting cast as well, and while the bulk of the narrative takes place in the summer of 1927, it's necessary to backtrack occasionally to set up an event that would take place that year.<br /><br />The importance of the summer of 1927, according to Bryson, is that it was the moment when America began to become dominant in the world for the first time. Our influence via movies, sports, war, aviation, and radio was overwhelming and lasting. Of course it's arbitrary to pinpoint a moment of change that precisely, and Bryson no doubt chose the year for its abundance of good stories.<br /><br />As entertaining as the book is, and it is an enjoyable book, I think I was more impressed by the google detours I took while looking for more information. There's a marvelous video on YouTube of the trip some American Legionnaires took to the convention in Paris in 1927. The video has been restored and it's so clear and vibrant, you're almost there yourself. Checking out silent film star Clara Bow's Brooklyn accent led to some clips of her in talkies and she sounds perfectly middle American, not at all like Fran Drescher, which you might conclude from Bryson's telling.<br /><br />Upshot-- Borrow the book and enjoy it at your leisure.vibrant, you're almost there yourself. 0064471837|5.0|This book is amazing. Its one I can return to over and over again. I first heard of the book from a friend who didn't care for it because she thought is was too dark.I couldn't help myself, I had to read it. After I did, I then made my entire family of 8 listen to it on a road trip, including my father who does not care for fantasy and is what you might call a literary snob. Everyone loved it. There are many reasons why this book is an amazing accomplishment but one of the stand out reasons for us was that so many of the fantasy novels out there set up mysterious characters with hidden powers but when it comes time for the big reveal one can't help but feel let down. When you travel through the arc of this story and reach the big reveals it delivers on the scale that was promised. I also think Mr. Nix has a fantastic ability to follow up the climax of the story. I was always completely interested in the epilogue and wanted to know as much about the characters he had made me fall in love with as possible. The themes are also very well done, so much depth was expressed through the different characters' journeys and discoveries. Many of the most ancient concepts of blood, music, power, death, chaos and order are well expressed here. The world that is created in these novels is believable and sucks you in and though it isn't done on the scale of novels like The Lord of the Rings or Game of Thrones, it achieves the same sort of reality and the language style used has the same integrity. It may be a little dark but it is also incredibly hopeful in my opinion. It deals with death, yes, and that is dark I suppose but even if you are the squeamish type these books are worth your time.

0525478817|5.0|THE FAULT IN OUR STARS is a book about young adults being forced to confront their own mortality from a relentless beast - cancer.  Hazel is a sixteen-year old cynical girl suffering from thyroid cancer with metastases to her lungs.  She can hardly make it up a flight of stairs without becoming short of breath.  She spends her life tethered to a portable oxygen tank.  The only reason she is still alive is because of an experimental chemotherapy drug that, so far, seems to be working.<br /><br />In an effort to keep Hazel's social life as normal as possible, her mother insists on her attending a cancer support group every Wednesday.  The purpose for Hazel's participation is much less about emotional support than about socialization.<br /><br />In Hazels words:<br /><br />ME: \\"I refuse to attend Support Group.\\"<br /><br />MOM: \\"One of the symptoms of depression is disinterest in social activities.\\"<br /><br />ME: \\"Please just let me watch American's Next Top Model.  It's an activity.\\"<br /><br />MOM:  \\"Television is a passivity.\\"<br /><br />ME: \\"Ugh, Mom, please.\\"<br /><br />MOM:  \\"Hazel, you're a teenager.  You're not a little kid anymore.  You need to make friends, get out of the house, and live your life.\\"<br /><br />ME:  \\"If you want me to be a teenager, don't send me to Support Group.  Buy me a fake ID so I can go to club, drink vodka, and take pot.\\"<br /><br />Needless to say, Mom wins, and Hazel goes to group.  This is where she meets Augustus, or Gus - a hotty cured from osteosarcoma.  The only tradeoff is that he now has a prosthetic leg.  A small price to pay for your life.<br /><br />The two begin to spend more time together.  Hazel introduces Gus to her favorite novel, AN IMPERIAL AFFLICTION, written by Peter Van Houghton.  The book details the story of a girl with cancer.  What haunts and consumes Hazel is that Van Houghton ends his masterpiece midsentence.  Hazel obsesses about finding out what happens to the characters.  Gus joins her in this quest.  He actually succeeds in contacting the author and arranging for he and Hazel meet the mysterious man.<br /><br />In a twist of fate, Hazel, Gus, and Hazel's mother are granted a trip to Amsterdam where they meet the reclusive, alcoholic, and ill-mannered writer.  The meeting is a bust.  Hazel leaves bitterly disappointed and without her long-awaited answers.  However, the trip is not a complete failure.  The time she spends alone with Gus gives them both treasures that are typically only bestowed upon adults.<br /><br />The ending, not surprisingly, is sad.  I don't consider that a spoiler.  How could such a book end otherwise?  But for the specifics, you will have to read it yourself.<br /><br />Just as AN IMPERIAL AFFLICTION was a gift to Hazel, THE FAULT OF OUR STARS was a gift to me, on many levels.  As a physician, it enlightened me as to what life is like for patients outside the walls of a hospital.  The world spins for them, just as it does for the rest of us.  Unfortunately, they have to deal with the same amount of crap we all do.  Life doesn't completely stop just because of cancer, but sometimes that's the beauty of it.  As a mother of a teenage daughter, I laughed at Hazel's adolescent attitudes and pushbacks.  In the next instant, I cried at what her disease had stolen from her.  John Green's research and authenticity was impeccable.  His ability to take such a heart-wrenching topic and balance it with humor, love, and growth proves he is genius.<br /><br />I purchased a Kindle copy of this book with no incentive or communication with the author or any of his representatives.  My opinions are honest and my own.actually succeeds in contacting the author and arranging for he and Hazel meet the mysterious man.<br /><br />In a twist of fate, Hazel, Gus, and Hazel's mother are granted a trip to Amsterdam where they meet the reclusive, alcoholic, and ill-mannered writer. 1451624468|1.0|It is an accurate sign of our decadent intellectual culture that a prominent publisher issues such a book. I agree with most of the one star reviews and add a few points. I have a Doctorate in Philosophy and have done research in the history of science; I taught philosophy for 20 years.  First, the two chapter titled \\"Nothing is Something\\" and \\"Nothing is Unstable\\" are shocking to a person who intuitively knows that beings exist outside his mind.  In grad school, I remember a course in Medieval Logic where the professor said the Medieval logicians held that 'if you begin your argument with a contradiction (eg. 'nothing is something'), then anything follows' meaning that you can say anything no matter how illogical. Krauss does just that. Second, he says that philosophy and theology have nothing to say about the meaning of life.  This is stunning, indicating that Prof Krauss thinks life as he conceives it is reduced to physics; however the average person must take on faith (on the authority of Dr. Krauss)the directly unobservable theoretical entities like particles and multiple universes as well as philosophical principles like 'Nothing is Something'.  Thus, religious faith and philosophical knowledge are replaced with faith in the physicist as his only guidance in life; but physicists disagree and so do the Darwinians, so whom do we follow? Third, it amazed me that there was no mention of Chance in the extensive index.  Fourth, Prof. Dawkins says in an Afterword that material particles \\"go into and out of existence like fireflies\\"; apparently it is just their nature to go back and forth from nothing to something which would indicate there is a real difference between Nothing and Something. As a former teacher of philosophy, I am convinced that the first principle of THOUGHT and REALITY is the Principle of Identity or Non Contradiction which goes back to Aristotle and forward through Aquinas and to the 20th century Thomists like Gilson, Maritain and Fr. Garrigou-Lagrange, who said frequently that the intellectual choice is between \\"God or Radical Absurdity\\"; this book exemplifies radical absurdity. As a conclusion I would say that Krauss' book is very bad philosophy mixed with some standard modern physics although I cannot judge the physics.  As an antidote to Krauss' book, one could read \\"The Devil's Delusion\\" by David Berlinski, \\"The Science Before Science\\" by Anthony Rizzi, and \\"The Quantum Enigma\\" by Wolfgang Smith (all I believe available through Amazon);  all the authors have great expertise in modern physics as well as philosophy.

006114665X|5.0|Mr. Clark explains that surviving documents are limited from the pre-war period. Those which would reveal embarrassing communications or implicate persons as initiators of the conflict have been destroyed or altered to present those people in a better light. Postwar history is dominated by the victor's argument that the Germans were to blame.<br /><br />The book details how minor conflicts in the 2 decades prior to the Great War created an atmosphere of paranoia and mis-interpretation of the intentions of Germany, Austria-Hungary, Serbia, Russia, and France. All of them were looking for allies with the mindset that fear would restrain any one country from acting while at the same time believing that war was inevitable as a means of solving diplomatic problems.<br /><br />I will try to summarize the evidence Clark has gathered. Serbia and Austria were competing for influence over the same territory and had become bitter enemies. Serbia was the silent partner in the assassination of Archduke Ferdinand who would probably have initiated a peaceful resolution after he became Emperor.<br /><br />France had loaned Russia money to build railroads to the German border. This would allow Russian troops to quickly engage the Germans. The French saw this as a counter to Germany invading France. But Germany saw that only a pre-emptive war soon would allow them to win. Austria moving against Serbia was seen as a manipulation by Germany to either defeat Russia or France. Austria banked on German support to keep the Russians out of the dispute. The Germans wanted Austria to hold off Russia while they defeated France and then took on the Russians.<br /><br />The Russian pre-mobilization was interpreted as the tripwire. The hawks in all capitals felt their views were vindicated and immediately pushed for war. Egotism combined with paranoia left little doubt that some kind of major war was inevitable and all the major powers had been arming for it for years.<br /><br />Personal comment: History is rife with Heads of State and generals thinking that a war would be quickly won. Most lasted years and only temporarily settled disputes. Alliances were fleeting. These lessons were not learned by those in power in 1914 nor afterward.<br /><br />Clark has collected a trove of official and personal correspondence that paints a much broader picture of the backdrop to the war. This is far more accurate and unbiased than the history taught in schools.

0399159347|5.0|In this multi-layered page-turner, three women struggle with unbearable situations. Cecilia Fitzpatrick is an ultra-organized wife, mother and Tupperware salesperson living in Sydney, Australia. She enjoys a happy marriage with her husband, John-Paul, sharing the joys of parenting their three quirky daughters. When one of those daughters develops a fascination with the Berlin Wall, it leads Cecilia into her attic to search for a chunk of the wall she acquired as a 20-year-old on a jaunt through Europe.<br /><br />The attic is well-organized but too close; John-Paul, suffering from claustrophobia, refuses to go into it. The only part of the attic that Cecilia has failed to organize is a stack of shoeboxes in which John-Paul saves each year's financial records. Although finding her bit of the Berlin Wall quickly, she accidently knocks down the tower of shoeboxes and must gather up the contents. That's when she finds something decidedly curious: a business-sized envelope inscribed in John-Paul's handwriting:<br /><br />For my wife, Cecilia Fitzpatrick<br />  To be opened only in the event of my death<br /><br />Cecilia is charmed at first, but then wonders if her husband knows something dire about his health. She mentions the envelope to John-Paul, who reacts very strangely. He begs her not to open it, claiming to be embarrassed. However, her daughters comment on their father; one claims she saw him crying, while the other makes an observation that Cecilia can't ignore. She is torn between her promise to John-Paul and her duty as a wife and mother. The letter inevitably will be opened, and the secret inside will alter everything in Cecilia's world.<br /><br />Meanwhile, another man divulges a secret to his wife. Tess O'Leary's world has revolved around her business partnership and relationships with her husband, Will, and her cousin Felicity. The three have formed a tight-knit family that includes Tess and Will's young son, Liam. When Will and Felicity tell Tess that they have something they need to say, she imagines it has to do with the advertising agency they share. Instead, the two people she is closest to devastate her, informing her that they have fallen in love. With her life shaken to the core, Tess takes Liam to stay with her mother in Sydney. To her amazement, when she enrolls Liam in St. Angela's, the local school, she discovers Connor Whitby, an ex-boyfriend, teaching PE.<br /><br />The school secretary at St. Angela's is a woman named Rachel Crowley, who is well-known in the area, partly because her teenage daughter was murdered more than two decades earlier. Although the crime was never officially solved, Rachel believes Connor to be the murderer. Meanwhile, the only part of her life that has given her joy recently is about to be removed, when her son and daughter-in-law take her grandson along on a move to New York.<br /><br />THE HUSBAND'S SECRET is the ultimate page-turner. How riveting is it? I devoured it in one deliciously unfettered day, unable to stop reading on and on. Author Liane Moriarty capably handles her cast of characters, weaving their stories together into a fascinating tapestry. These women are fully three-dimensional, and readers will experience a rollercoaster of emotions with them. Cecilia's story is particularly compelling; once she reads the forbidden letter, all bets are off. There is no predicting how the story could possibly end, and I predict no reader will manage to resist plunging onward.<br /><br />Reviewed by Terry Miller Shannon

B008JFUNWS|1.0|As far as the film genre of sci-fi fantasy goes, it might be time to say enough is enough - for the time being, at least.  Between Harry Potter, Lord of the Rings, Twilight, The Host, Beautiful Creatures, and any other franchise with a bunch of teen drama and whacky creatures running amuck, it's pretty safe to say the films of this particular genre are growing increasingly stale.  This genre of film has gotten so ridiculously predictable that if you've seen Harry Potter, you've essentially already seen the Twilight films and so on and so forth.  Seriously, how many different stories can possibly be told about the \\"chosen one?\\"  Each and every one of these films, including a beloved franchise like Star Wars, recycles the same old story about prophecy and destiny to the point that you'd think these authors and filmmakers would be tired of making stories about the same old thing.  Come to think of it, it's no wonder authors, like J.K. Rowling, Stephanie Meyer, and Rick Riordan, have all been named in plagiarism lawsuits in recent years.  When everyone's stories look alike, sound alike, and end alike - what did they expect to happen?  And, speaking of recycled stories - Percy Jackson is back with the film series' second installment, Percy Jackson: Sea of Monsters.<br /><br />Based on the novel of the same name (by Rick Riordan), Percy Jackson: Sea of Monsters is directed by Thor Freudenthal (Diary of a Wimpy Kid) and stars Logan Lerman as Percy Jackson - the demigod son of Poseidon.  An attack penetrates the walls of Camp Half-Blood, forcing Percy, his newfound Cyclops half-brother, Tyson (Douglas Smith), and his friends, Grover (Brandon T. Jackson) and Annabeth (Alexandra Daddario), to leave the camp on a mission to retrieve the Golden Fleece to restore the mystical barrier.  Meanwhile, Percy's former friend and current nemesis, Luke (Jake Abel), has his own plans as he and his followers are also on a mission to secure the fleece.  Leven Rambin, Stanley Tucci, Nathan Fillion, and Anthony Head also star in supporting roles.<br /><br />In all honesty, Percy Jackson & the Olympians: The Lightning Thief provided a great deal of entertainment - incorporating the gods of Greek mythology into present day.  While the first Percy Jackson film greatly resembled the events of the early Harry Potter films, the Percy Jackson character still had a great deal to offer regardless of the easy comparisons.  Like Potter, Jackson struggled with the idea that the world was full of mythical beings, along with the weight of being the \\"chosen one.\\"  Also like Potter, he relied heavily on his friends to help guide him through his journey and to help him become this potentially great leader of \\"destiny.\\"  Unfortunately, the main problems with Percy Jackson is he's not as popular as Harry Potter, doesn't have the drive or ambition of Frodo, and his sword isn't as cool as a lightsaber.  And frankly, his sidekicks - Grover and Annabeth - are not nearly as loveable as Ron and Hermione.<br /><br />On paper, Percy Jackson: Sea of Monsters provides a solid, well thought out storyline.  The idea of Percy Jackson being challenged again after the showdown in New York is an inevitable occurrence, but the problem with the sequel is that he was challenged too much in the first film and not challenged enough in the sequel.  In the first film, there's a massively threatening potential from the Greek gods to go to war with one another.  Let's be honest, the second film's plot relies solely on the journey to acquire a blanket.  That's right - the majority of this film follows these powerful characters as they travel across the United States to find a blanket, which happens to be resting on the shoulder of a giant, grumpy Cyclops - who lives in an amusement park.  The last film had lightning, gods, and a trip to Hades, while this sequel has absurd, blind taxi drivers, followed by an eventual trip to the oceanic version of the Pit of Sarlacc (from Return of the Jedi for those that don't know).  Sadly, there's no Boba Fett - or Amelia Earhart, in the belly of this water-based beast.<br /><br />Most (not all) bad movies at least have a few positives to admire.  Although admiration probably isn't the right word to use, but in any event, this film does have an early visit from a pretty sweet Transformer-like bull that shoots fire and does some major damage to Camp Half-Blood.  When Michael Bay gets a look at this thing, he'll probably wish he would have thought of it first - possibly having it transform from a Red Bull delivery truck (after all, product placement and transformers go hand-in-hand).  Aside from the bull, this sequel is also paid a visit from not one, but two Buffy: The Vampire Slayer alums.  Anthony Head takes over for the inexplicably absent Pierce Brosnan in the role of Chiron and Nathan Fillion plays the role of Hermes, the messenger of the gods who poses amusingly as a glorified UPS clerk.  Regardless, it would appear someone in the casting department has some deep admiration for Joss Whedon.<br /><br />It's clear the Percy Jackson novels have a substantial fan base, and 99 percent of the time, a film is unable to fully grasp the emotion of a novel.  The knock on this film has nothing to do with the novels, which have attained their own praise and devotion.  Still, it's painfully obvious this film sequel bumbles around from beginning to end, feeling unorganized and at times - just downright fake.  The CGI in the film is nothing to write home about, and while the cast is moderately entertaining (due largely to the addition of the mean-spirited character work of Leven Rambin), they still cannot make up for the poorly adapted script and bad direction.  Thor Freudenthal takes over for the Harry Potter alum, Chris Columbus - and it shows.<br /><br />Unfortunately for the Percy Jackson film franchise, this sequel loses any kind of \\"mojo\\" that was built in the first film, inevitably leading to this this dreadful and at times unbearable sequel.  The addition of a female lead, a bunch of zombies, and a golden blanket are simply not enough to maintain the average level of entertainment provided in the series' predecessor.  Still, the readers of Percy Jackson are ages 10 and up, so kids will easily find more entertainment in this film than adults.  The absence of the gods, Hollywood star power - not to mention an actual sea of monsters, is detrimental to the outcome of this film.  If you haven't yet invested in this film franchise, do yourself a favor and keep it that way.  But, if you're looking to acquaint yourself with Percy Jackson - hit the books.<br /><br />GRADE: D<br />FNDNreview.comse that don't know). B000028U0Y|5.0|There are very few albums that influence music the way this one has.  I was 14 years old when this album was released in 1968.  I can remember playing that vinyl LP so much I literally wore it out, not to mention my Dad got sick of hearing it so much.  The beauty of this version is that it restores the original concert, complete and in the original order, adding back the songs that were cut from the 1968 record because of time constraints of the vinyl LP's used at the time.  It also presents the concert complete with NO censorship, as was common in 1968.  You hear everything that happened at the concert, \\"colorful metaphors\\" and all!  This is also a brand new digital master from the original master tape, so audio quality is excellent.  As primitive as recording was at the time, they apparently used some very good and very expensive tape recorders for this concert, because the quality in transition to the CD format is amazing. Producer Johnson and his recording Engineer, Charlie Bragg, overcame the huge problem of \\"live sound\\" in the all-concrete cafeteria at Folsom by grouping all of the microphones together on stage, as close to the performers as possible, and then going direct into the two four-track machines with no \\"EQ\\" at all.  The resulting recording is stunning.  It lets you focus on what's important......the music.  And it is awesome......almost beyond description it's so good.  This has to be one of the top 100 albums in history.  There are very few positive things that came out of 1968..........Apollo 8 was one of them......this recording is definitely another.  Absolutely essential for anyone's music collection.

B00COCY67A|4.0|Starting with his '68 Comeback Special, a reawakened Elvis conjured a remarkable late-career hot-streak that included 1969's From Elvis in Memphis, the revitalized Vegas stage shows documented on That's the Way It Is and On Stage, and a return to his country, blues, gospel and rockabilly roots on 1971's Elvis Country. In January of 1973, Elvis stormed the airwaves with Aloha from Hawaii via Satellite, and soon after signed a new seven-year contract with RCA. In July and December of that year he booked himself into the legendary Stax studio on [[ASIN:B004SC8XHI McLemore Avenue]], adding to a string of Memphis studios that had been good luck charms: Elvis had launched his career at Sun, and revived his sense of self at Chip Moman's American Sound in 1969.<br /><br />The July sessions produced ten masters, eight of which were released on 1973's Raised on Rock, and two held back for 1974's Good Times. Four were also issued as singles, , with \\"Raised on Rock\\" climbing to #41 on the Hot 100, Tony Joe White's \\"I've Got a Thing About You Baby\\" peaking at #4 country, and \\"Take Good Care of Her\\" making the Top 40 AC. All ten of the masters were solid, though by no means extraordinary. Elvis was in good voice, but neither the material nor the band assembled from road regulars and Memphis guests sparked anything really deep. Elvis connected well with bluesier material like \\"Just a Little Bit\\" and Leiber & Stoller's \\"If You Don't Come Back,\\" and gospel-tinged backing vocals add weight to a few ballads, but the sessions never lift off in the way of his earlier work at American Sound. Two tracks - \\"Girl of Mine\\" and \\"Sweet Angeline\\" - swapped in players from the Stax house band, including the MG's rhythm section of Donald \\"Duck\\" Dunn and Al Jackson, but you'd barely know it from the final outcome.<br /><br />The December sessions were a great deal more productive, both in final output - 18 finished masters - and in musical vitality. The results were split across 1974's Good Times and 1975's Promised Land, further dissipating the sessions' unity and squandering the marketing value of \\"Elvis at Stax.\\" But even with the inept marketing, the sessions turned out three Top 20 hits on each of the pop and country charts, and a country chart topping album in Promised Land. Elvis sounds much more deeply engaged than he had in July, and the material and arrangements are a great deal stronger. Highlights include a fiery take on Chuck Berry's \\"Promised Land,\\" the strings, horns and deep bass of \\"If You Talk in Your Sleep,\\" the gospel-funk \\"I Got a Feelin' in My Body,\\" Jerry Reed's revival-charged \\"Talk About the Good Times,\\" and feeling covers of \\"Good Time Charlie's Got the Blues\\" and \\"You Asked Me To.\\" Two ballads, \\"It's Midnight\\" and \\"Loving Arms,\\" feature deeply touching, standout vocal performances.<br /><br />Beyond the twenty eight masters, this 3-CD set includes a generous helping of alternate takes and one unfinished track. All of this material has been released before, but scattered across a number of posthumous collections and expanded reissues. Augmented with bits of studio chatter, the outtakes give a more organic view of Elvis' presence at Stax than did the dispersed master takes. What you'll hear is an artist who's really committed to most of the material, and though the master takes were chosen for their commercial viability, the alternates are filled with vitality. Unlike the many soundtrack sessions through which Elvis often sleepwalked, and despite the Stax sessions being the product of a contractual obligation, Elvis was ready to make great music of his own volition. Freed from the confines of Hill & Range's catalog, Elvis drew from both longtime suppliers and contemporary songwriters, recording songs with which he felt a personal resonance.<br /><br />That personal resonance also applied to the assembled players, who were drawn from Elvis' road band and key Memphis and Muscle Shoals players such as guitarist Reggie Young and bassistNorman Putnam. But the results weren't as deeply impacted by Southern soul as were the earlier sessions at American Sound; Stax, it turned out, was more of a conveniently located venue than a sound with which Elvis wanted to engage. The label's legendary musicians were barely involved in the July sessions, and not at all in December. By the time the later dates came around, even the Stax recording equipment had been swapped out in favor of RCA's mobile unit, leaving the converted movie theater studio as Stax's only real participation. Still, Elvis was home in Memphis, riding the crest of a remarkable career resurgence, and mostly (modulo the Colonel's lingering machinations) in control.<br /><br />The 3-CD set is delivered in an 8x8 box that includes a deluxe 42-page booklet stuffed with photos, ephemera and notes by Roger Semon and Robert Gordon. The discs are screened with images of tape reels, and slid into the pockets of a tri-fold cardboard insert, from which fans will likely want to relocate them to jewel cases or other appropriate storage. Collectors who already own [[ASIN:B000009NSW Rhythm and Country]] and the FTD reissue of [[ASIN:B000RGUH46 Raised on Rock]], [[ASIN:B003YCLRI0 Good Times]] and [[ASIN:B006ZYVFMW Promised Land]] will have most of the tracks in this set, though having them all together in one (affordable!) place produces a uniquely coherent view of the sessions. One thing that becomes clear is that Elvis had a great album in him, but a contract that demanded two albums and multiple singles per year dug deeper than the sessions could support. What's great here is really great, and what's good is still passable. Though he'd record more in 1975-76, these Stax sessions are the last major sessions in his remarkable comeback. [2013 Hyperbolium]Norman Putnam. But the results weren't as deeply impacted by Southern soul as were the earlier sessions at American Sound; Stax, it turned out, was more of a conveniently located venue than a sound with which Elvis wanted to engage. The label's legendary musicians were barely involved in the July sessions, and not at all in December. By the time the later dates came around, even the Stax recording equipment had been swapped out in favor of RCA's mobile unit, leaving the converted movie theater studio as Stax's only real participation. Still, Elvis was home in Memphis, riding the crest of a remarkable career resurgence, and mostly (modulo the Colonel's lingering machinations) in control.<br /><br />The 3-CD set is delivered in an 8x8 box that includes a deluxe 42-page booklet stuffed with photos, ephemera and notes by Roger Semon and Robert Gordon. 0064471837|5.0|With the premise of this book in mind, I wasn't so sure it would be something I would enjoy - but I was really pleasantly surprised.  I usually dislike books which heavily use undead creatures because the creatures are typically so hollow and more resemble natural disasters with crude, carnal motivation - rather than sentient, calculating antagonists. Additionally, death is usually a passive verb ... something that happens to you while you are busy and only the aftermath of the verb is acknowledged. It was actually quite nice to see death as both a place and a process - an inert set of rules and tiers that can be tampered with with the correct tools or powers - but it isn't broken if its influence is escaped - much like gravity. Bells can work with it but can't permanently change it, it carries on, as it always has. This layer of dimension was entrancing and took away and sense of heavy morbidity, despite the fairly copious carnage throughout the book.<br /><br />My favourite addition to this story is Mogget - a creature who seems somewhat bitter but rather resigned to his fate so much that a pure feline nature overtakes him from time to time - however, he is not unlike what one would suspect a sentient cat would be like anyway. B0072AYJFI|5.0|I have read the Abhorsen trilogy about once a year since they first came out. I can't get enough of Nix's world or his characters. These books are usually considered YA because of the age of the characters--18-ish--and the coming of age themes they explore, but I'd hesitate to classify them so neatly. Yes, you can (and should) give them to your teens to read, and they can justifiably be found in high school libraries. But there's more to these books than that. The characters are deep and resonant, and each one will connect in a different way to anyone who has ever struggled to meet responsibilities that seem overwhelming, to fit in in a world where you don't feel like you belong, to figure out who you really are when everyone around you thinks they have the answer to that, or to open your mind in the face of new evidence or ideas. On top of all that stunning character work is the world itself: a modern, Enlightenment world of philosophy and science living side by side but slightly out of sync with a world of magic, legend, and spirit--both of them utterly real, and both of them needing each other in order to triumph over evil.<br /><br />Another thing I love about Nix's worlds, both this one and the other-dimensional world of the Keys to the Kingdom series--is that they are centered around the power of words. In the Keys series, whole creatures and landscapes are literally made of words, and only the right words provide the power to liberate or limit. In the Abhorsen series, the whole of existence is based on the Charter, the metaphysical series of sacred words and symbols that focus and limit the forces of magic in the world. There is Charter Magic, a Tao-like force into which people are baptized, and in which people share for the good of all nature and humanity, and then there's Free Magic, those beings and forces that refuse to discipline themselves or to limit themselves for the sake of the common life of all people and creatures. Each is controlled and expressed by words--Charter Marks, rune-like symbols that convey power. The Ideal being presented is that those who submit themselves to the common good, and those who pursue only selfish goals no matter the cost to others, each perform their acts of power through the ultimate, incontrovertible power of words. And really...how else is it ever done?<br /><br />I have recommended this series to countless teens and adults, and will continue to do so. In fact, I haven't read it in a while, so I may just get my own books out and read it again, for the third time this year.d by words--Charter Marks, rune-like symbols that convey power. The Ideal being presented is that those who submit themselves to the common good, and those who pursue only selfish goals no matter the cost to others, each perform their acts of power through the ultimate, incontrovertible power of words. And really...how else is it ever done?<br /><br />I have recommended this series to countless teens and adults, and will continue to do so. In fact, I haven't read it in a while, so I may just get my own books out and read it again, for the third time this year.

However, I changed my mind numerous times and felt torn about so many of the issues in the story.  I can see why people love this book or hate this book and there really isn't a lot of in-between.  I don't need to love the characters to love a book, sure it helps, but I don't' need to if the story is there.  I liked this book so much because the story was there.  But if you have to love the characters to love the book this might not be for you.  Don't get me wrong they were likeable, understandable but definitely and totally full of flaws.  I was kept on the edge of my seat with what could possibly happen next.<br /><br />Here is as much as I think I can say without ruining it for anyone.  Nick and Amy met fell in love and got married.  They were the best versions of themselves for a while they lead a charming life together.  But life happened, time went on and five years later they are not the same people anymore.  Nick hasn't really been a great husband for some time and Amy vanishes on their 5 year anniversary under unusual circumstances.  In the aftermath the story unfolds to reveal Amy and Nick's life together and what might have happened to Amy.  Yep, that is about all I can say.<br /><br />Gone Girl is a rollercoaster ride, with small details dished out here and there.  This is smart and wickedly intriguing.  I don't think there is anyone who can say completely oh yeah I saw that coming.  Because even what I thought I saw coming didn't end up being anything close to what the truth of it was.for a while they lead a charming life together. 0307245306|5.0|Percy Jackson is having trouble in the sixth grade. He seems to be failing all of his classes (again) and has been diagnosed with ADHD and dyslexia. On top of that, he is always a target for bullies, which to make life even more embarrassing, are often girls. But strange things have been happening recently that Percy can't explain, and when he tries to talk to his only friend, Grover, about them, Grover acts like nothing is out of the ordinary. Percy's home life is not great, either, since his step-dad is a selfish loafer who doesn't like Percy. His mom says his real dad went away on an ocean voyage many years ago and hasn't come back, but Percy thinks she's hiding something. When monsters from Greek mythology attack, he knows something is definitely wrong. But those are just stories...right?<br /><br />One of my friends kept telling me I needed to read this series, so I finally picked it up and listened to the book on CD. I loved it. It started out a little slowly for me, and I wasn't always sure where the story was going since it jumped around to different scenes so much, but no matter what, I wanted to know what would happen to Percy and his friends. Even though I'm not up on Greek mythology, that wasn't a problem. In fact you learn about it as you travel with Percy to meet the various gods and monsters. I enjoyed watching Percy overcome each trial put in his path and see him come to trust his instincts and his friends, despite being warned otherwise. The book broaches some dark subjects that may be scary for younger readers, so I recommend this book for ages ten and up. Anyone who enjoys a good adventure or quest story would probably like this first in a series. I already have the second one ready to listen to. A note on the audio version: very entertaining and great for car rides. The actor who does the reading changes voices well.
